Mr. Wright:

In accordance with the Interagency Agreement between the California Department of Toxic Substances Control (DTSC) and the California Department of Transportation (Caltrans), we are pleased to submit this Remedial Design Implementation Plan (RDIP) - Interim Phase 1 for the Caltrans Modesto Soil Stockpiles (the Site) located south of the State Route (SR) 99/Kansas Avenue interchange in Modesto, Stanislaus County, California.

This RDIP has been prepared to describe the technical approach and provide detailed plans for implementation of the Final Remedial Action Plan for the Caltrans Modesto Soil Stockpiles. The DTSCapproved remedial alternative for the barium-containing soil stockpiles is containment by incorporating the stockpiles as highway embankment fill and covering with structural pavement section and imported clean fill during construction of the SR-132/SR-99 interchange portion of the SR-132 West Project. This RDIP addresses Interim Phase 1 of the SR-132 West Project planned for completion in 2020. An additional RDIP will be prepared for the Ultimate Phase 2 portion of the project planned for completion in 2028.

Please contact the undersigned should you have any questions regarding this RDIP.

# REMEDIAL DESIGN IMPLEMENTATION PLAN - INTERIM PHASE 1

## 1.0 INTRODUCTION

This Remedial Design Implementation Plan (RDIP) - Interim Phase 1 has been prepared by Geocon Consultants, Inc. on behalf of the California Department of Transportation (Caltrans) for the Caltrans Modesto Soil Stockpiles (the Site) located south of State Route (SR) 99/Kansas Avenue interchange in Modesto, Stanislaus County, California (Vicinity Map, Figure 1). The California Department of Toxic Substances Control (DTSC), in cooperation with the Central Valley Regional Water Quality Control Board (CVRWQCB), is the lead regulatory agency providing site mitigation oversight under Caltrans Interagency Agreement Task Order No. 4, Amendment No. 1, dated June 17, 2016.

This RDIP has been prepared to describe the technical approach and provide detailed plans for interim implementation of the Final Remedial Action Plan (RAP, Geocon 2018) that was approved by DTSC on March 14, 2018. The selected remedial alternative to mitigate exposure to the barium-containing (and to a lesser extent lead-containing) soil stockpiles is containment by incorporating the stockpiles as highway embankment fill and covering with structural pavement section and imported clean fill during Interim Phase I and Ultimate Phase 2 construction of the SR-132/SR-99 interchange portion of the SR-132 West Project. This RDIP is specific to that portion of the SR-132 West Project that contains the three bariumcontaining soil stockpiles (Stockpiles 1 through 3) during Interim Phase 1 construction.

The SR-132 West Project will result in the ultimate build-out of a four-lane expressway by 2028. Interim Phase 1 of the project includes construction of the SR-132 West/6th Street and SR-132/East/5th Street extensions, two of four traffic lanes from east of SR-99 to North Dakota Avenue, the Carpenter Road interchange, and the SR-132 roadway structures across Emerald Avenue and SR-99 by 2020. Ultimate Phase 2 construction includes highway widening to four traffic lanes, construction of structures to accommodate the roadway widening along SR-132, and the SR-99/SR-132 interchange with related improvements along SR-99 by 2028.

The soil stockpiles (also referred to hereinafter as barium-containing soil), portions of which contain elevated levels of barium and lead, are planned to be contained within the project by utilizing them as embankment material within the overall lateral limits of Stockpiles 1 and 2 for roadway construction and associated retaining wall and bridge abutment backfill materials. Cut/fill grading will be necessary during Interim Phase 1 to properly consolidate and contain the existing soil stockpiles.

### 1.1 Site Description

The Site consists of three separate soil stockpiles within Caltrans right-of-way (ROW) located south of the SR-99/Kansas Avenue interchange, which are planned to be used for the SR-132 West Project. The following is a summary of the configuration, orientation, size, and surrounding vicinity of each stockpile:

- **Stockpile 1** is located south of Kansas Avenue and west of Emerald Avenue. It is approximately 600 feet long in the east-west direction, 160 feet wide, and has an estimated fill volume of approximately 34,000 cubic yards (yd3 ). It is bounded by commercial/light industrial development to the north and single-family residential to the south. To the west is vacant SR-132 ROW, and to the east is an approximately 240-foot-long vacant section of SR-132 ROW extending to Emerald Avenue.
- **Stockpile 2** is located south of Kansas Avenue, between Emerald Avenue and SR-99. It is approximately 1,650 feet long in the east-west direction, 160 feet wide, and has an estimated fill volume of approximately 102,000 yd3 . It is bounded by commercial/light industrial development to the north and single-family residential to the south. To the west is Emerald Avenue, and to the east is SR-99.
- **Stockpile 3** is located south of Kansas Avenue and east of SR-99. It has a curvilinear shape extending northwest to southeast, concave to the southwest, with a length of approximately 1,100 feet and a width of approximately 120 feet. It has an estimated fill volume of approximately 24,000 yd<sup>3</sup> . It is bounded by SR-99 to the south and west and commercial/light industrial development to the north and east. The Modesto Irrigation District Lateral #4 canal concrete box culvert extends beneath its southeastern end.

The stockpiles primarily comprise layered, poorly graded sand and silty sand similar to underlying native alluvial deposits of the Modesto Formation. The average maximum stockpile fill thickness is approximately 20 feet. Depth to groundwater measured in site-related monitoring wells in April 2018 ranged between approximately 35 to 46 feet (below natural grade) with flow generally toward the south (Geocon 2018). Groundwater extraction/dewatering is not anticipated during construction of the SR-132 West Project in the immediate vicinity of the soil stockpiles.

The stockpiles are currently enclosed within security fencing and bordered by adjacent property boundary fencing/walls or structures. The stockpiles, ROW boundaries, groundwater monitoring well locations and surrounding vicinity are depicted on the Site Plan, Figure 2.

### 1.2 Site History

From the 1930s to 1970s, property beneath and northeast of the SR-99/Kansas Avenue Interchange was occupied by chemical processing facilities operated by Food Machinery and Chemical Corporation (FMC) and its predecessors. Ores and minerals including barite (barium sulfate) and celestite (strontium sulfate) were processed for use in greases, lubricating oil and pigment blanks. Sodium sulfide was generated as a by-product and sold as a caustic and reagent. From the 1950s to the 1970s, liquid residue ("tailings") generated at this facility was discharged to unlined evaporation ponds. In 1961, the State purchased a 4.3-acre parcel in the southwestern portion of the FMC facility, including a portion of the ponds, for the construction of the SR-99 freeway through Modesto. Pond tailings and underlying soils from the FMC property along with native soils excavated south of the SR-99/Kansas Avenue interchange were subsequently placed to create Stockpiles 1 through 3.

An Initial Site Assessment completed for Caltrans for the SR-132 West Project in 2003 identified a potential for the soil stockpiles to contain residual chemicals associated with the former FMC impoundments. A Preliminary Site Investigation completed in 2004 and subsequent site characterization studies performed for Caltrans confirmed the presence of elevated barium concentrations (and other contaminants of potential concern [COPCs]) in stockpile soil samples exceeding regulatory health-based screening levels. The results of groundwater monitoring activities at the Site indicated that the identified COPCs were reported at concentrations less than California Maximum Contaminant Levels for drinking water. The results of a 2007 Human Health Risk Assessment (HHRA) and 2013 HHRA Update prepared for Caltrans indicated that the soil stockpiles do not pose an unacceptable risk or hazard to current or future offsite residents, trespassers, construction workers or hypothetical future shallow groundwater users.

In a letter dated December 17, 2009, the DTSC stated that:

*"DTSC finds that the soil stockpiles, as currently managed by Caltrans on Caltrans property, do not pose a risk to human health for: 1) Caltrans workers who access the fenced site to conduct mowing operations, conduct fence repairs, or other routine activities; 2) trespassers; and 3) residents adjacent to the stockpiles. Until such time that the State Route 132/99 Interchange project is constructed and/or the final disposition of the soil stockpiles is determined, Caltrans should continue to manage the soil stockpiles by: 1) limiting access to Caltrans authorized personnel; 2) inspecting and maintaining the chain-link fence; 3) prohibiting any activities involving excavation/grading, off-site removal of soil, or placement of other soil on the Site; and 4) maintaining the current grade and vegetative cover. Caltrans should also maintain the existing groundwater monitoring system associated with the Site."* 

To date, the only stockpile grading/removal action completed at the Site was excavation and landfill disposal of approximately 2,800 yd3 of the northern portion of Stockpile 3 in 2012 under DTSC oversight as part of Caltrans' rehabilitation of the SR-99 northbound off-ramp to Kansas Avenue to improve traffic safety and meet current design standards. The highway safety improvement project included widening the off-ramp shoulder areas and associated drainage features. Shoulder widening on the east side of the off-ramp included construction of a retaining wall following partial removal of the Stockpile 3 embankment slope. The results of air monitoring completed during the Stockpile 3 remedial excavation activities indicated that airborne levels of barium and lead were well below regulatory thresholds.

A Feasibility Study (FS) and RAP were prepared for the Site in 2014 and 2018, respectively, and subsequently approved by DTSC. The FS evaluated four remedial alternatives including No Action, Institutional Controls, Removal, and Containment. Based on the alternative evaluation criteria, the DTSC-approved long-term remedial measure to mitigate potential exposure to the soil stockpiles is "Alternative 4 - Containment" to be implemented during Interim Phase 1 and Ultimate Phase 2 construction of the SR-132 West Project. As outlined in the RAP, containment of the stockpiles will be achieved by utilization/consolidation of the soil stockpile material generally within the existing stockpile footprint as highway embankment fills, and retaining wall and bridge abutment backfill, and covering with Caltrans-maintained structural pavement section and/or imported clean fill material.

### 1.3 RDIP Objectives and Schedule

This RDIP has been prepared to present the remedial design, barium-containing soil management procedures, and construction monitoring and regulatory reporting protocols to be implemented during interim containment (encapsulation) of the soil stockpile material in general accordance with the criteria and requirements presented in the Final RAP. This RDIP is specific to soil stockpile containment measures to be implemented during Interim Phase 1 construction of the SR-132 West Project. An additional RDIP will be prepared for the Ultimate Phase 2 portion of the project.

The following SR-132 West Project Interim Phase 1 schedule is anticipated:

RDIP Final Approval: Early 2019 Project Design Approval: Early 2019

Contractor Bid Award: Early to Mid 2019

Start Barium-Containing Soil Containment: Mid 2019 Complete Barium-Containing Soil Containment: Late 2019 Complete Interim Phase 1 Construction Late 2020 Remedial Completion Report Approval: 2021

### 1.4 RDIP Document Organization

Following this Introduction, the RDIP contains the following sections and contents:

- **Section 2.0 Project Organization** describes the project team organizations and representatives, and roles and responsibilities.
- **Section 3.0 Barium-containing Soil Containment Design**  summarizes the soil stockpile containment design details.
- **Section 4.0 Containment Design Implementation** summarizes the soil stockpile containment implementation criteria including barium-containing soil management.
- **Section 5.0 Monitoring Plan**  presents stormwater, health and safety, and air monitoring requirements during Interim Phase 1 highway construction in the vicinity of the soil stockpiles.
- **Section 6.0 Regulatory Reporting** addresses regulatory reporting requirements.
- **Section 7.0 Post Construction Monitoring/Maintenance** describes monitoring and maintenance activities that would be performed to ensure that the implemented containment measures continue to be effective.
- **Section 8.0 Project Websites and References** provides a list of websites and references cited.

# 2.0 PROJECT ORGANIZATION

This section describes the role and responsibilities of the following project team organizations and representatives responsible for implementation of the RAP and this RDIP during Interim Phase 1 construction of the SR-132 West Project:

**Site Owner/Responsible Party:** State of California/Caltrans

**Caltrans' Environmental Consultant:** Geocon Consultants, Inc.

**Regulatory Agencies:** DTSC and CVRWQCB

**SR-132 West Project Proponent:** City of Modesto (City)/Stanislaus Council of Governments

**Project Proponent's Civil Engineer:** Dokken Engineering

**Project Proponent's Construction Manager:** to be determined

**Project Proponent's Highway Construction Contractor:** to be determined

## 2.1 Project Team Responsibilities

Caltrans is responsible for the implementation of the RAP and this RDIP under regulatory oversight and approval by DTSC in cooperation with the CVRWQCB. Caltrans and DTSC are further responsible for public outreach and participation.

DTSC reviewed the July 18, 2018 Draft RDIP prepared by Geocon and prepared a Conditional Approval Letter dated August 20, 2018 (Appendix A). The DTSC letter provides conditional approval of the Draft RDIP pending inclusion of administrative (non-technical) text revisions and review of the 95% and 100% design plans. DTSC reviewed the September 14, 2018 RDIP prepared by Geocon that incorporated the recommended text revisions and prepared a Conditional Approval Letter dated October 12, 2018 (Appendix A). This RDIP includes applicable excerpts of the 100% design plans (Appendix C). A complete set of the 100% design plans and final project specifications will be submitted to DTSC and the CVRWQCB in early 2019.

Geocon, under contract with Caltrans, is responsible for verifying that the highway construction work associated with the soil stockpiles is performed in substantial conformance with the RAP and RDIP requirements. Specifically, Geocon will:

- Supervise the proper abandonment of site-related groundwater monitoring wells impacted by planned Interim Phase 1 highway construction;
- Perform annual groundwater monitoring of the remaining site-related groundwater monitoring wells;
- Observe and photo-document barium-containing soil excavation, fill placement and capping activities;
- Perform barium-containing soil removal verification soil sampling and analysis;

- Perform proposed clean soil import source sampling and analysis;
- Perform worker zone and perimeter air monitoring;
- Perform periodic stormwater monitoring including observations and sampling;
- Review RDIP requirements with the construction manager and highway construction contractor;
- Interact with and periodically update the Caltrans Environmental Manager and DTSC and CVRWQCB Project Managers;
- Provide monthly status reports; and
- Prepare a Remedial Action Completion Report.

The City is responsible for Interim Phase 1 and Ultimate Phase 2 project design and construction. Dokken, under contract with the City, will provide final design and construction specifications for the SR-132 West Project. The City's construction management firm and highway construction contractor will be responsible for executing the following work associated with the management of barium-containing soil with oversight coordination by Caltrans and Geocon:

- Worker health and safety (awareness training);
- Mobilize equipment, material and personnel;
- Site grading and retaining wall/bridge structure construction;
- Barium-containing soil removal/consolidation within designated areas;
- Management of placed barium-containing fill material;
- Dust control;
- Stormwater best management practices; and
- Placement of pavement and approved imported clean cover soil and vegetated ground cover over designated barium-containing soil consolidation areas.

# 3.0 BARIUM-CONTAINING SOIL CONTAINMENT DESIGN

This section summarizes design details for the containment of barium-containing soil during construction of Interim Phase 1 of the SR-132 West Project.

## 3.1 Selection of Remedial Alternative

The approved remedial alternative (containment) will ultimately contain the barium-containing soil stockpile material beneath roadway pavement and behind retaining walls and bridge abutments of the SR-132 West Project to eliminate direct exposure and to be protective of groundwater and surface water. As an interim measure, the barium-containing soil will also be contained beneath imported clean soil vegetated cap along the north sides of Stockpiles 1 and 2. The primary factors which supported the selection are: (1) this alternative is protective of human health and the environment and is technically feasible; (2) this alternative is cost-effective because funding is available for construction of the SR-132 West Project; and (3) this alternative will minimize the potential for contaminants to migrate to groundwater or to be eroded by stormwater runoff.

## 3.2 Soil Stockpile Containment

Containment of the soil stockpiles will be achieved by their use as highway embankment for the SR-132/SR-99 interchange portion of the SR-132 West Project which is the reason the stockpiles were originally placed on the Site in the early 1960s.

The stockpiled soil will be contained behind retaining walls and bridge abutments and beneath roadway pavement/hardscape. As described in Section 1.0, the project will be constructed in two phases - Interim Phase 1 to be completed by 2020 and Ultimate Phase 2 to be completed by 2028. Interim Phase 1 of the project includes constructing a two-lane highway over Stockpiles 1 and 2. During this phase, the northern slope areas of Stockpiles 1 and 2 will not be contained behind retaining walls and beneath pavement/hardscape, but will be contour graded for drainage and capped with a minimum 12-inch-thick vegetated, clean soil cap. Retaining walls will be constructed along the northern ROW boundary of Stockpiles 1 and 2 during Ultimate Phase 2 construction resulting in completed containment of barium-containing soil.

A portion of Stockpile 3 was originally planned to be encapsulated during Interim Phase 1 between retaining walls and structural pavement section behind the SR-132 bridge abutment on the east side of SR-99 and the remainder of Stockpile 3 transported for use as fill over Stockpiles 1 and 2. However, project design changes have resulted in elimination of the retaining walls behind the bridge abutment that were originally proposed for use as final containment for a portion of Stockpile 3. Therefore, Stockpile 3 will be completely removed and placed over Stockpile 1, and within adjacent vacant State ROW between Stockpile 1 and Emerald Avenue as permanent highway embankment fill.

### 3.2.1 ADL Contaminated Soil

In addition to containment of barium-containing soil, Stockpiles 1 and 2 designated fill areas may further be utilized for placement of aerially deposited lead (ADL) contaminated soil generated from planned highway widening excavations in the unpaved shoulder areas of northbound (NB) SR-99 between L Street and the Kansas Avenue off-ramp, and from any other identified lead-impacted soil excavation areas within the project boundaries.

ADL investigations completed in 2006 (Shaw 2006) and 2012 (Blackburn 2012) identified elevated lead concentrations in shallow soil along the unpaved shoulder areas of SR-99 north and south of Kansas Avenue. Total and soluble lead concentrations for some samples exceed California and Federal hazardous waste criteria.

The ADL soil will be placed in accordance with the 2016 *Soil Management Agreement for Aerially Deposited Lead -Contaminated Soils* between DTSC and Caltrans. "Clean soil" is defined as soil, based on a 95 percent upper confidence limit (95% UCL), containing total lead less than or equal to 80 milligrams per kilogram (mg/kg) and Waste Extraction Test (WET)-soluble lead less than 5.0 milligrams per liter (mg/l), and not containing other constituents at concentrations that pose an unacceptable threat to human health or the environment. "ADL-contaminated soil" is defined in the DTSC Agreement as excavated soil, based on a 95% UCL, that contains total lead greater than 80 mg/kg and/or WET-soluble lead greater than or equal to 5.0 mg/l. ADL-contaminated soil reused under the DTSC Agreement must always be at least five feet above the highest groundwater elevation and, depending on lead concentrations, may need to be covered with at least one foot of clean soil or a pavement structure. ADL-contaminated soil may not be placed in areas where it might contact groundwater or surface water (such as streams and rivers), and must be buried in locations that are protected from erosion that may result from stormwater runoff. Additionally, ADL-contaminated soil shall not be placed in or covered by soil with a pH less than 5.0. ADL-contaminated soil having a pH less than or equal to 5.0 may not be reused and must be properly disposed of. A tabular summary of the DTSC Agreement conditions regarding the reuse and management of ADL soil and a copy of the 2016 DTSC Agreement are in Appendix B.

Caltrans personnel confirmed with the DTSC Project Manager that the completed ADL soil placement areas within the Stockpile 1 and 2 barium-containing soil containment zones will not require separate as-built survey data.

### 3.2.2 Stockpile Removal and Fill Areas

Figures 3-1 through 3-5 depict plan views of existing Stockpiles 1 through 3 and planned removal areas on the SR-132 West Project design grading plans. The NB SR-99 shoulder ADL removal area is depicted on Figure 1.

The barium-containing soil stockpile removal areas and associated estimated removal volumes include the following:

Stockpile 1 - no planned removal

Stockpile 2 - Emerald Avenue bridge abutment (2,200 yd3 ) and SR-99 bridge abutment (1,650 yd<sup>3</sup> )

Stockpile 3 - complete removal (24,000 yd<sup>3</sup> )

**Total estimated barium-containing soil removal volume = 27,850 yd3**

Figures 3-1 through 3-3 depict the following designated barium-containing soil and ADL fill consolidation areas at Stockpiles 1 and 2 with associated estimated fill capacity volume estimates:

Stockpile 1 - upper surface and southern slope area (15,000 yd<sup>3</sup> )

State ROW - between Stockpile 1 and Emerald Avenue bridge abutment (12,500 yd3 )

Stockpile 2 - upper surface and southern slope area (27,000 yd<sup>3</sup> )

**Total estimated barium/ADL consolidation area volume = 54,500 yd3**

Based on these total estimated quantities, approximately 26,650 yd3 of soil stockpile consolidation area is available for fill placement of ADL soil.

Figures 4a and 4b present typical Stockpile 1 and 2 cross sections of completed Interim Phase 1 construction. The cross-sections depict:

- Existing stockpile soil (to remain in place) over native soil.
- Existing stockpile soil to be removed for the eastern abutment of the Emerald Avenue Overcrossing.
- Designated barium-containing soil and ADL consolidation zones (fill placement areas) over the upper stockpile surfaces, extension of southerly stockpile slopes, and between Emerald Avenue and Stockpile 1.
- Construction of a mechanically stabilized earth (MSE) retaining wall along the southern SR-132 ROW, the Emerald Avenue Overcrossing, and associated imported clean backfill materials based on required geotechnical soil strength parameters.
- Placement of minimum 12-inch-thick clean cover fill material over the barium-containing soil and ADL consolidation zones. As an alternative, minimum 4-inch-thick aggregate base (AB) materials may be placed on the upper stockpile surface pending subsequent placement of structural pavement and hardscape.
- Placement of structural pavement and hardscape over the entire upper stockpile surface.
- Establishment of erosion control (non-irrigated natural vegetation hydroseed) on the northerly capped stockpile slopes.

Portions of the 100% SR-132 West Project design plans that depict plan and elevation views of the soil stockpile removal and containment areas are in Appendix C.

The Ultimate Phase 2 buildout will include construction of an MSE retaining wall along the northerly SR-132 ROW adjacent to Stockpiles 1 and 2 to accommodate additional travel lane pavement and hardscape. Clean imported fill material will be placed over the northerly capped stockpile slopes with minimal disturbance (if any) to the barium-containing soil and ADL consolidation zones. Construction of the Ultimate Phase 2 buildout will complete final encapsulation of barium containing soil within Stockpiles 1 and 2.

## 3.3 Stockpile Removal Verification

The western and eastern ends of Stockpile 2 in the vicinity of proposed bridge abutments, and entire Stockpile 3 will require removal and placement within the designated barium-containing fill consolidation zones. In order to document that the stockpile material has been removed, verification soil sampling and analytical testing will be performed.

DTSC does not publish screening levels for barium. The San Francisco Regional Water Quality Control Board (SFRWQCB) Tier 1 (unrestricted land use) Environmental Screening Level (ESL) for barium is 3,000 mg/kg. The DTSC's Human and Ecological Risk Office (HERO) Note 3 residential (unrestricted land use) screening level for lead is 80 mg/kg. In addition to being protective of human health risk exposure, the CVRWQCB requested that the stockpile material removal verification thresholds be evaluated for groundwater protection. To address this request we completed an analysis of the historical total and soluble barium and lead soil data using conservative assumptions under the Designated Level Methodology. The results of this analysis are presented in a July 3, 2018 Technical Memorandum (Appendix D).

Based on this information, the soil stockpile removal area analytical data will be compared to the following human health exposure and groundwater protection verification thresholds:

 Barium - 1,000 mg/kg Lead - 80 mg/kg (DTSC residential screening level)

# 4.0 CONTAINMENT DESIGN IMPLEMENTATION

This section describes how the removal, consolidation and containment of barium-containing soil (and ADL contaminated soil) at Stockpiles 1 through 3 will be implemented during Interim Phase 1 construction of the SR-132 West Project.

## 4.1 Groundwater Monitoring Well Protection/Abandonment

Groundwater monitoring wells MW1 through MW10 associated with the Caltrans Modesto Stockpile Project (Figure 2) are sampled on an annual basis typically during the month of April. Well locations MW2 and MW5 on the southern sides of Stockpiles 1 and 2 will be buried beneath highway embankment fill and future highway travel lanes so these wells will require proper abandonment prior to the start of highway construction activities. Wells MW1, MW3, MW7 and MW8 are located in areas of future drainage improvements (i.e. drainage ditches and ponds) and will also require proper abandonment prior to the start of highway construction activities. The remaining four monitoring wells (surface well completions) will be protected in place by the highway construction contractor and made available for annual sampling events during highway construction. The highway construction contractor will be responsible for protecting wells MW4, MW6, MW9 and MW10 from being buried and/or damaged by grading equipment/vehicles (i.e. protective bollards, steel plates, barricades, etc.) and repairing or replacing any well damage during the highway construction activities.

Caltrans/Geocon will abandon monitoring wells MW1, MW2, MW3, MW5, MW7 and MW8 subsequent to the April 2019 annual monitoring event under Stanislaus County permit requirements. The wells will be properly abandoned by pressure-grouting in general accordance with the requirements of California Well Standards Bulletin 74-90, Monitoring Well Standards, Part III, as required by Stanislaus County.

To pressure grout, the California C-57 licensed driller will initially fill each well with neat Portland cement, sand-cement grout or other acceptable material having a permeability of less than 10 feet per year. The well seal material will be placed by tremie from the bottom of the well under sufficient pressure and length of time to penetrate the annular filter pack. An additional one third of the well casing volume of seal material is anticipated to be pumped into the well to ensure sufficient sealing of the well's annular pack and screen.

Following pressure-grouting, the top 5 feet of each well will be over-drilled and that portion of the well casing removed. The over-drilled borings will then be filled with 21-sack Portland cement or 10-sack sand/cement slurry to the ground surface. Debris generated from the well abandonments (casing, concrete, standpipe, MW5 bollards, etc.) will be contained for appropriate offsite disposal and/or recycling/reuse. Soil cuttings will be either placed in 55-gallons drums for offsite landfill disposal or incorporated within the Stockpile 1 and 2 barium-containing soil consolidation zone.

The need and timing for replacing the abandoned monitoring wells at other designated location(s) will be determined by Caltrans in coordination with the CVRWQCB.

## 4.2 Project Scoping Meetings

The City and Caltrans provided complete sets of 65% and 95% design plans to DTSC and the CVRWQCB with the July 2018 Draft RDIP and September RDIP and have provided opportunity for DTSC and CVRWQCB to participate in Caltrans' constructability review process. The City and Caltrans will provide a full set of the 100% Interim Phase 1 design plans (including relevant project specifications) when completed in early 2019.

The City and Dokken will provide a briefing of this RDIP and associated barium-containing and ADL soil management and containment responsibilities, monitoring protocols and regulatory/community involvement during the project pre-bid meeting to inform prospective highway construction contractors of project related scoping and bid item costs.

After contractor award and prior to the start of construction, a RDIP project scoping meeting will be held to discuss the barium-containing and ADL soil excavation, placement and containment activities, dust mitigation and monitoring, health and safety, project scheduling and other related topics. Attendees at the RDIP scoping meeting will include City, Caltrans, Geocon, DTSC, construction management and highway construction contractor representatives.

DTSC will prepare a "Start Work Notice" in English and Spanish for publication in the local newspaper(s), other appropriate public repositories, and the project websites listed in Section 8.0 two weeks prior to the start of Interim Phase 1 highway construction.

## 4.3 Permitting/Utility Clearance

The highway construction contractor will be responsible for obtaining any required permits prior to commencing with earthmoving activities including any required dust control/mitigation permits with the San Joaquin Valley Air Pollution Control District.

Although no utilities are anticipated to be present within the footprint of Stockpiles 1 through 3, if any subsurface utilities could be affected by the construction project, they will be addressed prior to construction with those specific utility owners. Standard utility clearance precautions such as obtaining Underground Service Alert notification ticket prior to excavating will also be taken.

## 4.4 Barium-containing Soil Excavation and Fill Placement Area Preparation

Stockpile 1 through 3 clearing operations performed by the highway construction contractor will include removal and proper offsite disposal of any remnant homeless encampments, debris materials, and perimeter fencing in planned highway grading/improvement areas.

Prior to any excavation or fill placement of barium-containing soil, the surface of Stockpiles 1 through 3 will be mowed to a minimum remaining vegetation thickness of two inches. Designated bariumcontaining soil consolidation fill placement area surfaces will then be disced/ripped, moistureconditioned, and recompacted per project geotechnical specifications.

A representative of Geocon will be onsite fulltime during any site preparation, excavation, fill placement and clean fill containment of barium-containing soil. Air monitoring for potential fugitive dust emissions, as described in Section 5.3, will also be implemented during these activities.

## 4.5 Barium-containing Soil Excavation and Fill Placement

The following presents a summary of designated barium-containing soil excavation and consolidation fill placement areas:

**Stockpile 1** - no barium-containing soil excavation is planned for Stockpile 1. Barium-containing soil consolidation fill placement zones include the upper surface and southern slope area of Stockpile 1, and existing vacant ROW between Stockpile 1 and the Emerald Avenue bridge abutment as depicted on Figures 3-1 and 3-2.

**Stockpile 2** - barium-containing soil excavation planned for Stockpile 2 includes the western end (Emerald Avenue bridge abutment) and eastern end (SR-99 bridge abutment). Anticipated excavation depths range from approximately 10 to 20 feet to provide for "clean" construction of planned bridge abutments and to ensure the barium-containing soil is placed behind the retaining wall along the southern ROW boundary at Stockpile 2. The western end of Stockpile 2 will be excavated to the native ground surface elevation of approximately 80 feet above mean sea level. The eastern end of Stockpile 2 will be excavated to the native ground surface elevation of approximately 82 feet above mean sea level. Bariumcontaining soil consolidation fill placement zones include the upper surface and southern slope area of Stockpile 2 between the two bridge abutments. The designated Stockpile 2 barium-containing soil excavation and consolidation fill placement zones are depicted on Figures 3-2 and 3-3.

**Stockpile 3** - complete removal of barium-containing soil is planned for Stockpile 3 as depicted on Figures 3-3 through 3-5. Anticipated Stockpile 3 removal excavation depths will extend to an estimated maximum depth of 13 feet to the native ground surface elevation of approximately 84 feet above mean sea level.

Figures 4a and 4b present typical cross sections of Stockpiles 1 and 2 following completed Interim Phase 1 including barium-containing and ADL soil consolidation zones and containment measures.

Excavation, transport and fill placement of barium-containing soil will be performed by the highway construction contractor using conventional grading equipment. Barium-containing soil excavated from Stockpile 3 will be carefully loaded in covered (tarped) haul trucks (i.e. no exposed soil) for transport to the designated Stockpile 1 and 2 consolidation fill placement zones. The designated truck haul routes between the Stockpile 3 removal area and the Stockpiles 1 and 2 fill placement zones are depicted on Figure 5. Following loading, each truck will be observed for any overspill soil on the vehicle that requires removal prior to transport. The haul truck cleaning/decontamination procedures implemented by the highway construction contractor will be monitored by Caltrans' environmental consultant to ensure that the barium-containing soil is properly loaded for transport.

All transported barium-containing soil will be delivered to the designated Stockpile 1 and 2 fill placement zones for direct placement/compaction as permanent highway embankment fill. **Temporary stockpiling of barium-containing soil will not be permissible.** 

Recordkeeping related to movement and placement of the stockpile soil will be the responsibility of the highway construction contractor. Construction inspection records related to fill compaction and survey data will be maintained by the project inspection firm and surveyor with copies provided to the highway construction contractor, the City and Caltrans.

Time lapse photography will also be utilized to document excavation and placement of bariumcontaining fill and clean capping operations at Stockpiles 1 through 3. Professional grade time-lapse camera(s) will be utilized by the highway construction contractor to generate dated still images and highdefinition time lapse movie(s) of the stockpile grading and associated highway construction activities. The digital images and movie(s) will be the property of Caltrans. Specific details regarding the time lapse photography requirements will be provided in the project non-standard construction specifications.

## 4.6 Verification Sampling and Analysis

The soil stockpile removal activities will be overseen by a Geocon California Professional Geologist (PG) or a field geologist/engineer working under the direct supervision of a PG. The field representative will determine when the designated soil stockpile removals have been completed based on survey data compared to documented original ground surface elevations, observations for native soil conditions, and stockpile thickness and perimeter soil data generated during prior site investigation studies. The individual performing the oversight will also be responsible for preparing and maintaining daily field logs that, at minimum, document the personnel onsite, activities performed, where air monitoring is taking place, whether visible dust is observed, description of active soil stockpile excavation, record quantities of materials excavated, and confirmation of removal area limits (confirm native soil conditions). Written daily field reports will be supplemented by photographs as applicable. The individual performing the oversight will also collect stockpile removal verification samples and prepare accompanying chain-of-custody documentation.

The completed removal of barium-containing soil at the eastern and western ends (bridge abutment areas) of Stockpile 2 and entire Stockpile 3 will be determined by monitoring targeted excavation depths based on original ground surface elevations, observations by Geocon's Project Geologist, and verification soil sampling and analytical testing. Verification soil samples will be obtained from the completed barium-containing soil excavation areas (including loading, unpaved haul roads and track-out prevention areas outside of Stockpiles 1 and 2) at the rate of one sample per 5,000 square feet of removal area and one sample per 100 lineal feet of activity area. The soil samples will be obtained from the exposed excavation soil surface using hand-sampling methods (new and precleaned stainless trowels) and placed in new laboratory-provided glass containers, capped, labelled, and delivered to a California-certified analytical laboratory using chain-of-custody protocol. The verification samples will be submitted for analysis of barium and lead using Environmental Protection Agency (EPA) Test Method 6010B with a targeted reporting limit of 1.0 mg/kg. The verification soil sample analytical results will be compared to the threshold levels of 1,000 mg/kg for barium and 80 mg/kg for lead. The stockpile removal activities will be confirmed completed upon receipt of verification soil sample analytical data (total values or calculated 95% UCLs) that is less than the threshold levels.

The following table provides a summary of original ground surface elevations provided by Caltrans and the minimum number of verification soil samples (i.e. sufficient data set for statistical analysis) to be obtained from each of the stockpile excavation areas:

| Excavation Area      | Original Ground Surface Elevation (Above Mean Sea Level) | Minimum Number of Verification Samples |
|----------------------|----------------------------------------------------------|----------------------------------------|
| West End Stockpile 2 | 80                                                       | 8                                      |
| East End Stockpile 2 | 82                                                       | 12                                     |
| Stockpile 3          | 84                                                       | 24                                     |

Verification soil samples will further be obtained from any truck loading areas located outside the footprint of the stockpile excavation areas.

## 4.7 Grading Control and Containment Measures

The highway construction contractor will be responsible for maintaining proper dust control, erosion control, and stromwater best management practices (BMPs) in accordance with project design, Caltrans specifications and the approved Stromwater Pollution Prevention Plan (SWPPP) during the highway grading activities. Anticipated BMPs include runoff and erosion control, storm drain inlet protection and soil track-out prevention per Caltrans' standard specifications. It is anticipated that water truck/spray will be sufficient to properly maintain dust control (no visible dust) in areas of soil excavation, hauling on unpaved surfaces and in fill placement areas. **Grading within barium-containing soil will be suspended during periods of high winds, when dust control measures are determined to be inadequate to control generation of visible dust, or where uncontrolled water runoff or soil trackout is observed until acceptable corrective measures are implemented. Caltrans' environmental consultant in coordination with the construction manager will have stop work authority if any of these conditions arise during barium-containing soil grading operations.** 

The highway construction contractor shall provide survey data of the final barium-containing soil containment zones (including ADL soil and clean cover materials) within Stockpiles 1 and 2. The survey data shall include precise latitude, longitude and elevations (North American Vertical Datum 1988), and corresponding SR-132 postmile limits (approximate SR-132 stations 1125+60 through 1131+95 [Stockpile 1] and 1135+90 through 1148+30 [Stockpile 2]) for Caltrans' use in recording a regulatory-required land use covenant (LUC)/deed restriction with the Stanislaus County Clerk-Recorder Office along with the original Assessor's Parcel Number(s) associated with that portion of the highway alignment. Per DTSC, a LUC is only required for the completed barium-containing soil containment zones. The completed soil stockpile removal areas including the western and eastern ends of Stockpile 2 and removed Stockpile 3 will not require a LUC.

The surface of the completed Stockpile 1 and 2 barium-containing soil and ADL consolidation zones (including east- and west-facing temporary slopes) will be capped with minimum 12-inch-thick clean fill material consisting of approved imported fill and/or minimum 4-inch-thick AB materials (pending placement of structural pavement section, hardscape and/or additional clean embankment fill). The proposed source of clean imported fill soil consists of currently vacant and agricultural land within planned excavation areas along the SR-132 ROW between the Carpenter Road and Rosemore Avenue overcrossings as depicted on Figure 1. The specific clean fill source areas (once defined by the highway construction contractor) will be sampled by Geocon for laboratory analysis in general accordance with DTSC's *Information Advisory Clean Imported Fill Material* (Appendix E) for pre-approval by DTSC prior to placement. Construction geotechnical inspectors will confirm proper barium-containing and clean imported fill compaction through observation and in-place density testing.

The cleaned capped northerly slopes of Stockpiles 1 and 2 will be vegetated using a native plant mix hydroseed (i.e. compost, hydroseed, fiber roll and hydromulch) per Caltrans' standard specifications that will not require ongoing irrigation systems. The slope vegetation (and any associated erosion control and drainage features) will be maintained by Caltrans until the Ultimate Phase 2 portion of the project completes final containment of barium-containing soil (i.e. retaining wall and highway pavement) along the northerly portions of Stockpiles 1 and 2.

# 5.0 MONITORING PLAN

This section presents a summary of planned stormwater, health and safety, and air monitoring activities associated with barium containing soil removal and placement activities during Interim Phase I construction of the SR-132 West Project.

## 5.1 Groundwater/Stormwater Monitoring

Caltrans/Geocon currently perform groundwater and stormwater monitoring at the soil stockpiles that will continue during Interim Phase 1 construction activities. Groundwater monitoring activities are performed on an annual basis (usually April) in general accordance with monitoring protocols presented in the DTSC-approved *Final Work Plan, Groundwater Assessment* prepared by Shaw Environmental, Inc., and dated January 2006 (Shaw, 2006).

Stormwater sampling and analytical testing is typically performed during qualified precipitation events to evaluate potential runoff conditions at the soil stockpiles in general accordance with monitoring protocols presented in the DTSC-approved *Final Surface Water Sampling and Analysis Plan (SAP),*  prepared by Shaw Environmental, Inc. dated January 2006 (Shaw, 2006) and Geocon's *Addendum to Surface Water Sampling and Analysis Plan,* dated February 20, 2013 (Geocon, 2013). The monitoring events include five sampling locations along the perimeters of the soil stockpiles and two background locations. These monitoring events will continue during Interim Phase 1 construction and may incorporate additional or revised sampling locations. However, these sampling events are specific to the soil stockpiles and are not intended to replace or address the highway construction contractor's responsibilities for stormwater protection as outlined in the project specifications and SWPPP.

## 5.2 Health and Safety Plan

Although most of the COPCs have been demonstrated to be present in the stockpiles at concentrations generally less than residential health risk screening levels (and therefore much less than commercial/industrial or construction worker screening levels), barium and lead are present at elevated concentrations. A health and safety plan (HSP) has been prepared for Geocon personnel and as a guide to other site workers to discuss the COPCs and appropriate precautions to limit exposure to them for onsite workers and nearby residents and businesses by implementing measures to control dust generation (water spray) and confirmation of this by air monitoring during construction. The HSP (Appendix F) covers health and safety precautions for other worker hazards unrelated to the COPCs such as heat illness, lifting of heavy objects, slip/trip/fall hazards, equipment safety, and provides emergency contacts and routes to the nearest hospital emergency room.

Work at the Site will be performed in accordance with applicable State and Federal Occupational Health and Safety Standards set forth in 29 Code of Federal Regulations, Sections 1910 and 1926; and California Health and Safety Regulations as set forth in Title 8, California Code of Regulations, and guidance by DTSC. Contractors and other site workers/visitors shall be provided a copy of the Geocon HSP for informational purposes but are expected to follow health and safety procedures developed specific to their work activities in accordance with project specifications addressing required contractor-prepared HSP and Lead Compliance Plan.

Grading and other soil-related construction activities within the soil stockpiles will not be required to be performed by Occupational Safety and Health Administration (OSHA) 40-hour health and safety trained personnel or contractors with Class A-HAZ licenses. However, health and safety awareness training will be provided through an initial site meeting and during daily tailgate safety meetings

## 5.3 Air Monitoring

Perimeter air monitoring will be performed during all site activities that involve disturbance (surface preparation, excavation, loading, transport, fill placement, etc.) to document total airborne particulate concentrations and to assess the effectiveness of the highway construction contractor's dust control measures. If the results of air monitoring for specific work activities demonstrate that dust control measures are effective and that there is no exposure to COPCs in the stockpiles via airborne dust, then the required frequency of monitoring may be decreased to periodic monitoring with the approval of DTSC.

The air monitoring program will include:

- Monitoring daily meteorological forecast to anticipate on site environmental conditions such as wind direction and speed;
- Notifying the highway construction contractor in the event a downwind real-time particulate counter exceeds a calculated Fence Line Total Dust Action Level or upwind background dust level alarm so corrective action can be implemented, if necessary; and,
- In addition to the 60 second data logging programmed in the real-time monitors, check each downwind real-time air monitor instrument every 30 minutes and the upwind monitor(s) hourly to ensure proper operation, battery capacity, etc., and record the averaged dust reading in a daily log.

### 5.3.1 Action Level Determination

The risk of worker exposure to barium or inorganic lead-impacted soil during grading is considered low while performing earthwork using dust control methods in compliance with project specifications. As long as dust control is provided, airborne concentrations of barium and inorganic lead are anticipated to remain well below the California OSHA 8-hour time-weighted average Permissible Exposure Limit (PEL-TWA) of 10 milligrams per cubic meter of air (mg/m<sup>3</sup> ) of air for barium published in Title 8 California Code of Regulations (T8 CCR) §5155 Table AC-1, or the Action Level of 0.03 mg/m<sup>3</sup> as well as the PEL-TWA of 0.05 mg/m<sup>3</sup> for inorganic lead published in T8 CCR §1532.1.

Since workplace California OSHA exposure standards are neither established, nor intended to be used in evaluating risk to public health, it is not appropriate to use either the PEL for barium or inorganic lead in evaluating potential airborne exposures to the public for perimeter air monitoring for this project. Although the California OSHA PELs for barium and inorganic lead are not intended to assess exposure risk to the public, they can be used as a relative indicator of potential hazard (i.e., the lower the published PEL concentration the higher the potential exposure risk). Relative to their respective PEL-TWAs, barium at 10 mg/m3 represents less of a potential exposure hazard than inorganic lead at 0.05 mg/m3 . Therefore, real-time air monitoring will primarily focus on measurement of inorganic lead to document the effectiveness of engineering controls (wet methods) to suppress airborne dust.

The California Air Resources Board (ARB), in consultation with the Office of Environmental Health Hazard Assessment (OEHHA) has published a 30-day average ambient lead standard of 1.5 µg/m3 as a public health standard. Using a lead in stockpile soil concentration of 190 mg/kg as a conservative exposure risk for fugitive dust during this soil excavation project, ambient air monitoring will be conducted using one upwind and two downwind monitoring locations at the active soil stockpile grading area of the Site.

Based on the ARB-OEHHA airborne unit risk of 0.0015 mg/m3 , a Fence Line Action Level is calculated using the following formula and 190 mg/kg of inorganic lead:

Total Dust 
$$mg/m^3 = \frac{\text{(ARB-OEHHA unit risk for lead of } 0.0015 \text{ mg/m}^3\text{) x } (1,000,000 \text{ mg/kg})}{\text{(total lead concentration in soil of } 190 \text{ mg/kg})}$$

The calculated Fence Line Action Level for total dust above (upwind) background levels is 8 mg/m3 . Since this level is nearly the same as the California OSHA 8-hour PEL-TWA for total particulates, and using a safety factor of at least 0.5, a downwind Fence Line Action Level of 4 mg/m3 above upwind background dust levels will be used for ambient real-time air monitoring. The Fence Line Action Level of 4 mg/m3 is significantly more conservative than that calculated for barium (69 mg/m3 ) based on the California OSHA 8-hour PEL-TWA for barium of 10 mg/m3 .

### 5.3.2 Perimeter Air Monitoring Plan

Using a conservative total lead concentration of 190 mg/kg, the calculated Fence Line Action Level for a total airborne dust concentration above background (upwind) levels measured at the downwind perimeters of the excavation areas is 4 mg/m3 . As noted above, the Fence Line Action Level includes a safety factor of at least 0.5.

This Fence Line Action Level will be compared to real-time direct reading instrument measurements to ensure that the "wet methods" utilized during soil stockpile grading activities at the Site are effective in controlling the offsite migration of dust. Perimeter monitoring conducted during the project shall include one representative upwind (background) sample and two representative downwind (offsite) sampling locations. Air monitoring will be collected over either an 8-hour period, or the duration of the excavation, and soil handling and sampling tasks; whichever is shorter in duration.

Ambient air monitoring will be performed using MIE pDR-1200 real-time direct reading particulate counter with a PM-10 inlet and active sampling attachment for 37 mm filter cassettes using a personal sampling pump calibrated at 2.0 to 3.0 liters per minute. Pre-weighed 5 micron polyvinyl chloride filters (5µ PVC) attached to the pDR-1200 particulate counters will be analyzed for inorganic lead and barium compounds, and total mass. The use of pre-weighed 5µ PVC filters allows for both total particulate gravimetric and inorganic lead and barium analysis.

The air monitoring samples will be submitted for analysis to a laboratory accredited by the American Industrial Hygiene Association Industrial Hygiene Laboratory Accreditation Program. Air sampling and analysis will be performed in accordance with NIOSH 7300 ICP-Mass Spectrometry (7300-MS) or equivalent method using pre-weighed 5µ PVC filters.

The initial pre-weighed 5µ PVC filter samples collected for each representative work activity will be submitted to the laboratory for analysis of inorganic lead and barium under 24-hour turnaround time. Assuming reported levels of inorganic lead are less than ARB-OEHHA unit risk for lead of 0.0015 mg/m3 , and the Fence Line Action Level for total airborne dust concentrations above background do not exceeded 4 mg/m3 , all other 5µ PVC filter samples will be submitted to the laboratory for routine analytical turnaround time of from 5 to 7 business days.

The pDR-1200 real-time monitors will be calibrated according to the manufacturer's instructions and programmed to log total dust levels every 60 seconds. In addition, the audible alarm on the monitor located downwind of excavation, and soil handling and sampling activities will be set to the highest "Total Dust" level recorded on the ambient upwind monitor. An example air monitoring worksheet is in Appendix G.

# 6.0 REGULATORY REPORTING

## 6.1 Progress Status Reports

Periodic progress status reports (minimum monthly) will be prepared for submittal to Caltrans, City and DTSC to summarize the soil stockpile containment activities completed by the highway construction contractor, results of associated grading activity monitoring including confirmation soil sample and air monitoring data, and any variances to this RDIP. Separate reports will be prepared and submitted to DTSC for annual groundwater monitoring and periodic stormwater monitoring events.

## 6.2 Remedial Action Completion Report

A draft Remedial Action Completion Report will be prepared by a California Professional Engineer and submitted to DTSC approximately 30 days following the completion of the Interim Phase I soil stockpile monitoring activities. The Remedial Completion Report will contain the following information:

- Groundwater monitoring well destruction documentation;
- Observed conditions during stockpile grading/containment activities;
- Volume of soil stockpile material excavated and placed (based on transport truck counts);
- Results of stockpile removal verification samples and air monitoring activities;
- Stormwater and erosion control monitoring;
- Source, quantity and laboratory documentation for imported clean cover fill materials;
- Summary of completed Interim Phase I barium-containing soil and ADL containment;
- Observations, findings, and conclusions;
- Operation and maintenance requirements:
- Tabular summaries of soil and air sample analytical data;
- Figures (i.e. plan view and cross sections) depicting completing barium-containing soil and ADL removal and fill placement areas, and verification soil sample locations;
- Stockpile consolidation zone survey data and exhibits (i.e. signed and sealed as-built drawings);
- Site photographs;
- Air monitoring data sheets, and
- Laboratory reports and chain-of-custody documentation.

The Remedial Action Completion Report will be submitted to DTSC for review and approval and finalized upon receipt of DTSC's comments.

# 7.0 POST CONSTRUCTION MONITORING/MAINTENANCE

This section describes monitoring and maintenance activities that will be conducted following completed soil stockpile containment measures implemented during Interim Phase 1 of the SR-132 West Project.

## 7.1 Operation and Maintenance

Following completion of Interim Phase 1, Caltrans will enter into an Operation and Maintenance Agreement (OMA) with DTSC and prepare an Operation and Maintenance Plan (OMP) for DTSC's review and approval. The OMP will require annual inspection of the installed containment measures (travel lane pavement, hardscape and vegetated clean fill cover) to confirm the measures are properly maintained, intact and properly functioning as exposure barriers to the environment and direct contact. The OMP will further reference relevant sections of Caltrans' highway maintenance manual (http://www.dot.ca.gov/hq/maint/manual/maintman.htm). The annual inspections will also confirm that perimeter walls and fencing are effective in restricting access to authorized personnel only. The identification of, and implementation schedule for, any required corrective action measures will be included in annual inspection reports to be submitted to DTSC.

Annual groundwater monitoring, periodic stormwater monitoring, and submittal of annual inspection reports will continue at the Site until such time as the Ultimate Phase 2 of the SR-132 West Project is completed or the DTSC and CVRWQCB indicate that these monitoring activities are no longer necessary.

## 7.2 Land Use Covenant

A recorded LUC for the contained soil stockpiles, including a legal boundary survey, will be required by DTSC to restrict the types of land use and future activities that are allowed on the Site. The LUC will recognize that the proposed transportation land use is compatible and is acceptable from a health risk perspective. Unrestricted land uses (e.g., residential, schools, daycare, hospital, senior care, etc.) will not be allowed on the Site.

The LUC will be prepared consistent with DTSC policy and finalized and recorded with the Stanislaus County Clerk-Recorder Office after the containment measures are implemented and before the Site is certified by the DTSC as having been remediated. The LUC (including geospatial data that defines the Stockpiles 1 and 2 barium-containing soil and ADL placement limits) will run with the land and stay in effect as long as hazardous substances limit use of the Site and until terminated by the DTSC. Pursuant to Section 67391.1 of Title 22, Division 4.5, Chapter 39, CCR, the responsible party will pay all costs for DTSC oversight associated with administration of the LUC. The DTSC has authority to require modification or removal of any land improvements placed in violation of the restrictions. Violation of the LUC will be grounds for the DTSC to file civil or criminal actions as provided by law.

## 7.3 Five-Year Review

Caltrans will perform five-year reviews to assess the effectiveness of the interim and final soil stockpile containment measures during the project and after completion. The five-year reviews would focus on monitoring and maintenance of the implemented containment measures and potential for exposure to soil stockpile materials. Monitoring of groundwater and stormwater will have been ongoing and routinely reported to DTSC and the CVRWQCB and therefore would not be a focus of the reviews. DTSC will provide project certification following completion of the final containment measures during Ultimate Phase 2 of the SR-132 West Project.

The Department of Toxic Substances Control (DTSC) in consultation with the Central Valley Regional Water Quality Control Board (RWQCB) has reviewed the Draft Remedial Design Implementation Plan noted above (Draft RDIP) submitted by Geocon Consultants Inc. (Geocon) on behalf of the Department of Transportation (Caltrans). The DTSC and RWQCB comments provided on the preliminary document have been addressed but one additional comment is provided below:

 It is recommended that the title be changed to 'Remedial Design Implementation Plan – Interim Phase 1' to be consistent with sections of the document which describe the two phases of the road construction project. In addition, the Introduction section of the document should clearly indicate that this RDIP is specific to that area of the SR-132 West Project that consists of soil stockpiles 1,2, and 3.

Pending incorporation of the above recommendations and review of the 95% and 100% document submittals the Draft RDIP is conditionally approved.
